  в”Ӯ            в”Ӯ                    в”Ӯ toolchains, provisioning              в”Ӯ
  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

  ~/Workspace/ is your creation (or possibly originated from an IDE convention вҖ”
   VS Code, Xcode workspace files, etc.). It has no Apple-defined semantics. The
   Spotlight hit I found was just indexing your existing directory, not
  referencing a system template.

  вҳ… Insight в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  - macOS only hard-provisions ~8 directories. They're baked into
  NSSearchPathDirectory enum values and Finder's sidebar. Everything else in
  $HOME is user or app created.
  - The Developer/ directory is the closest analogue вҖ” Xcode creates it on first
   install вҖ” but even that is optional and app-initiated, not OS-initiated.
  - Your ~/Workspace/ has no Apple metadata protecting it (no com.apple.rootless
   xattr, no SIP protection). It's plain user space.
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ

  So there is no "Apple-intended ideal form" to recover or conform to.
  ~/Workspace/ is entirely yours to define.

вҸә ~/Developer вҖ” Ideal Form and Purpose

  The Beginning: NeXTSTEP вҶ’ Mac OS X 10.0 (2001)

  /Developer was born as a NeXTSTEP inheritance. When Mac OS X shipped in March
  2001, the Developer Tools installer (a separate CD, opt-in) created /Developer
   as the single centralized location for all development software: Project
  Builder, Interface Builder, SDKs, headers, examples, documentation,
  command-line toolchains.

  It was not provisioned by the OS itself вҖ” it appeared only when a developer
  explicitly chose to install the tools. This is the key distinction: /Developer
   was always elective infrastructure, not default furniture like ~/Documents.

  The NSSearchPathDirectory enum encoded this at the framework level from day
  one:
  - developerDirectory (raw value 6) вҶ’ resolves ~/Developer in user domain,
  /Developer in local domain
  - developerApplicationDirectory (raw value 3) вҶ’ resolves
  ~/Developer/Applications

  Both constants descend from NeXTSTEP's original path conventions.

  The Golden Era: /Developer (2003вҖ“2011)

  During Xcode 1.0 through 3.x, /Developer was a complete, self-contained 
  development environment:

  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ

  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ /Developer/Tools/         в”Ӯ CLI utilities                                в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ /Developer/Makefiles/     в”Ӯ Build system support                         в”Ӯ
  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

  Developers added /Developer/usr/bin to $PATH. The directory was the root of 
  the development world.

  The Ending: Xcode 4.3 (February 16, 2012)

  Apple eliminated /Developer entirely. Everything moved inside
  Xcode.app/Contents/Developer/. Three rationales:

  1. Mac App Store distribution вҖ” a .app bundle is the standard unit. The old
  "download installer from App Store, run it to populate /Developer" flow was
  broken UX.
  2. Delta updates вҖ” a single bundle enables incremental patching.
  3. Multiple installations вҖ” you can now have Xcode.app and Xcode-beta.app side
   by side, switching via xcode-select --switch. A single /Developer made this
  impossible.

  On first launch, Xcode 4.3 prompted users to delete the old /Developer. The
  era was over.

  The Afterlife: Three-Tier Split (2012вҖ“Present)

  What was one directory became three:

  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
  в”Ӯ           Location            в”Ӯ Owner  в”Ӯ            Contents            в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ                               в”Ӯ Xcode  в”Ӯ Toolchains, platforms, SDKs,   в”Ӯ

  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ                               в”Ӯ System в”Ӯ CommandLineTools,              в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ /Library/Developer/           в”Ӯ        в”Ӯ CoreSimulator runtimes,        в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ                               в”Ӯ (root) в”Ӯ DeveloperDiskImages вҖ” shared,  в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ                               в”Ӯ        в”Ӯ system-wide                    в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ                               в”Ӯ        в”Ӯ DerivedData (build             в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ ~/Library/Developer/          в”Ӯ User   в”Ӯ intermediates), CoreSimulator  в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ                               в”Ӯ        в”Ӯ devices, Xcode user settings вҖ” в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ                               в”Ӯ        в”Ӯ  mutable, per-user state       в”Ӯ

  ~/Developer Itself: The Ghost Form

  ~/Developer occupies a peculiar ontological position:

  - macOS recognizes it as a magic name. If you create ~/Developer/, Finder
  assigns it a hammer glyph icon from CoreTypes.bundle вҖ” the same treatment
  given to ~/Documents, ~/Downloads, ~/Music. This icon treatment works only at
  ~/Developer, nowhere else.
  - Apple never creates it. Unlike ~/Documents or ~/Desktop, no system process
  provisions it. It exists only if you make it.
  - The SDK constants that point to it are deprecated.
  NSSearchPathDirectory.developerDirectory is marked deprecated with the note:
  "There is no one single Developer directory."
  - No Apple documentation describes its intended contents. No WWDC session, no
  filesystem guide, no human interface guideline says what should live there.

  It is a recognized but uninstantiated Form вҖ” Apple encoded the concept into
  the framework enum, gave it an icon, then deprecated the pointer and never
  populated it.

  вҳ… Insight в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  - The trajectory is dissolution. /Developer began as a monolith (one directory
   = all tools), fragmented into a three-tier system (bundle + system + user),
  and left ~/Developer as a vestigial recognition вҖ” an icon with no mandate.
  - The NSSearchPathDirectory deprecation is the formal death certificate.
  Apple's reason вҖ” "There is no one single Developer directory" вҖ” is an
  ontological statement: the Form dissolved into particulars. The universal
  became multiple concrete instances inside .app bundles.
  - The magic icon is the only remaining trace of intent. It tells you Apple
  once planned for ~/Developer to be a canonical user-facing location, the way
  ~/Documents is for documents. That plan was never executed. The icon persists
  as archaeological evidence of an abandoned design.
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ

  The beginning was a monolith. The ending was dispersal. What remains is a name

  ---
  The Two Philosophies of Home

  macOS: "Users see documents, not implementation"

  Apple's home directory descends from NeXTSTEP's four-domain model (User вҶ’
  Local вҶ’ Network вҶ’ System). The design intent is editorial: the Finder mediates
   between raw filesystem and user perception, showing only what Apple believes
  users should see.

  The provisioned directories (what Apple creates for you):

  в”Ӯ Frameworks/, Fonts/,    в”Ӯ User-scoped overrides of system equivalents.  в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ Logs/                   в”Ӯ                                               в”Ӯ
  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

  Apple's architectural axioms:

  1. Configuration is an API, not a file. NSUserDefaults is the interface;
  .plist files are implementation details. This is why Library is hidden.
  2. The Library cascade is a search path. User overrides Local overrides
  System. SIP protects the bottom; hiding protects the top.
  3. Dotfiles are a Unix accident. Apple tolerates them. The Finder hides them.
  The HIG ignores them. Apple's own GUI apps never use them.
  4. Media segregation by type, not by project. Movies, Music, Pictures exist
  because Apple's apps (iMovie, Music.app, Photos) expect type-specific buckets
  вҖ” not because users naturally organize by media type.

  ---
  Windows: "Abstraction over paths, separation by roaming behavior"

  Windows user profiles descend from Windows 95's Shell Folders, through NT's
  domain model, to Vista's Known Folders system. The design intent is enterprise
   portability: data is classified by whether it should travel with the user
  across machines.

  The provisioned directories:

  Directory: Desktop/
  Since: Win 95
  KNOWNFOLDERID: FOLDERID_Desktop
  Design Intent: Physical backing of desktop namespace. Merged with
    Public\Desktop in shell view.
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  Directory: Documents/
  Since: Win 95 OSR2 (as "My Documents")
  KNOWNFOLDERID: FOLDERID_Documents
  Design Intent: User-created files. Canonical save target.
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  Directory: Downloads/
  Since: Vista
  KNOWNFOLDERID: FOLDERID_Downloads
  Design Intent: Browser/app download target. No CSIDL вҖ” arrived after that era.
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  Directory: Music/
  Since: Win 98 (inside My Documents)
  KNOWNFOLDERID: FOLDERID_Music
  Design Intent: Media bucket. Promoted to sibling in Vista.
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  Directory: Pictures/

  KNOWNFOLDERID: FOLDERID_Pictures
  Design Intent: Media bucket.
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ

  Directory: Favorites/
  Since: Win 95
  KNOWNFOLDERID: FOLDERID_Favorites
  Design Intent: IE bookmarks. Legacy artifact, still provisioned.
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ

  Directory: Links/

  KNOWNFOLDERID: FOLDERID_Links

  Directory: OneDrive/
  Since: Win 8.1
  KNOWNFOLDERID: FOLDERID_SkyDrive
  Design Intent: Cloud sync root.

  The hidden infrastructure (AppData/ three-tier model):

  Tier: AppData\Roaming
  KNOWNFOLDERID: FOLDERID_RoamingAppData
  Design Intent: Settings that follow the user across machines. Preferences, UI
    state, bookmarks. Copied via roaming profiles in AD environments. Must be
    small вҖ” traverses the network at logon/logoff.
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  Tier: AppData\Local
  KNOWNFOLDERID: FOLDERID_LocalAppData
  Design Intent: Machine-specific, non-essential data. Caches, compiled shaders,

    thumbnails, large temp data. Regenerated on new machines. Analogous to
    ~/.cache.
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  Tier: AppData\LocalLow
  KNOWNFOLDERID: FOLDERID_LocalAppDataLow
  Design Intent: Sandboxed process data. Created for Vista's Mandatory Integrity

    Control вҖ” IE Protected Mode runs at Low integrity and can only write here.
    Without this, browser sandboxing is impossible.

  Microsoft's architectural axioms:

  1. Programs should never hardcode paths. The Shell Folders вҶ’ CSIDL вҶ’
  KNOWNFOLDERID progression is a 30-year arc toward forcing path abstraction.
  Each generation exists because the previous one leaked implementation details.
  2. Separation by roaming behavior, not by type. The Roaming/Local/LocalLow
  split classifies data by what should travel with the user вҖ” more precise than
  XDG's model. This is an enterprise-first architecture.
  3. Type-based organization for users, location-based for apps. Vista promoted
  Music/Pictures/Videos from children of Documents to siblings вҖ” users think by
  type, not by hierarchy. Windows 7 Libraries took this further: virtual
  aggregation of physical locations.
  4. Backward compatibility as permanent geological debt. Junction points, Shell
   Folders registry keys, CSIDL wrappers вҖ” each generation adds a compatibility
  layer that can never be removed. The profile is a sediment record.
  5. No developer standard. No FOLDERID_Developer. Unix tools scatter dotfiles
  in %USERPROFILE%; Microsoft tools use AppData; nobody agrees. Win 11's Dev
  Drive (a separate ReFS volume) is Microsoft's first acknowledgment of this gap
   вҖ” but it's infrastructure, not a profile directory.

  ---
  The Gaps: Where Your Container Lives

  Both systems have the same structural seam:

  1. Apple designed for users who create documents and consume media. The home
  directory is Documents + Media Buckets + Hidden Library. There is no concept
  of "a person who builds systems."
  2. Microsoft designed for users who create documents and roam across 
  enterprise machines. The profile is Documents + Media Buckets + Roaming/Local
  split. The developer story is an afterthought (Dev Drive in 2023, already
  deprecated Dev Home in 2025).
  3. Neither system accounts for a meta-layer. Both assume the user works within
   their applications, saving into the provided buckets. Neither conceives of a
  user who designs the structure itself вҖ” who treats the directory tree as an
  ontological statement rather than a filing cabinet.

  The available insertion points on macOS:

  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”¬в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
  в”Ӯ           Location           в”Ӯ               Why it works               в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө

  в”Ӯ Any path outside ~/Library/, в”Ӯ These four are the only directories apps в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ  ~/Documents/, ~/Desktop/,   в”Ӯ  and iCloud interact with. Everything    в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ ~/Downloads/                 в”Ӯ else is inert.                           в”Ӯ
  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

  What Apple will never touch:
  - Any directory in ~/ that doesn't match a provisioned name
  - Any directory starting with . (hidden from Finder by convention)
  - Anything not referenced by an NSSearchPathDirectory constant

  What Windows will never touch:
  - Any directory in %USERPROFILE%\ that doesn't match a KNOWNFOLDERID
  - Any directory on a separate volume (Dev Drive model)

  вҳ… Insight в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  - Both operating systems designed their home directories as consumption 
  architectures вҖ” places to receive and organize output from applications.
  Neither designed for a user who is the system architect.
  - The "magic icon" directories (~/Developer/, ~/Sites/) are archaeological
  evidence of abandoned Forms вҖ” things Apple once intended but never
  instantiated. They are the closest either system comes to acknowledging that
  the home directory might need to be extensible.
  - Your ~/source--all-ever/ strategy is structurally sound: it exists in
  Apple's blind spot. macOS will never provision it, never sync it, never hide
  it, never touch it. It is outside the editorial layer. The same principle
  applies on Windows вҖ” any non-KNOWNFOLDERID directory in the profile root is
  invisible to the system.
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ

  ---
  The Design Principle for Your Container

  The terrain tells you three things:

  1. Don't fight the provisioned directories. They exist because apps expect
  them. ~/Documents/ will always be the Save dialog default. ~/Downloads/ will
  always receive browser output. Let them do their job.
  2. Don't build inside them. Anything in ~/Documents/ or ~/Desktop/ gets
  iCloud-synced, Spotlight-indexed, TCC-gated, and shown to every Save dialog.
  Your system should not live where applications expect to find user files.
  3. Build adjacent. A directory at ~/ level with a non-reserved name is:
    - Invisible to iCloud sync
    - Invisible to KNOWNFOLDERID / NSSearchPathDirectory
    - Invisible to Finder sidebar (unless you drag it there)
    - Visible to Terminal, to agents, to your tools
    - Given a generic folder icon (unless you pick a magic name like Developer/)

  Your container is the directory that is within the home directory but outside
  the OS's editorial model. It participates in the filesystem (it has a path, it
   has permissions, it exists) but it does not participate in the operating
  system's opinion about what a home directory should contain.

  That is the Form your source--all-ever occupies: present to the filesystem,
  absent from the system's self-concept.

вқҜ define the directories and folders of the apple universe as                   
ontological-envelopes                                                           

вҸә This requires no further research вҖ” I have the complete material. What follows
   is synthesis.

  ---
  Apple's Filesystem as Ontological Envelopes

  An ontological envelope is a bounded region of being defined not by its
  contents but by what kind of thing is permitted to exist within it. Each
  envelope has:

  - A membrane вҖ” the admission criterion (what may enter)
  - A governor вҖ” the authority that writes and seals
  - A visibility вҖ” who can perceive the interior
  - A durability вҖ” what happens to contents under pressure (disk space,
  migration, reset)
  - A relation вҖ” how it participates in adjacent envelopes

  ---
  Envelope Zero: The Volume Pair

  Since macOS Catalina (2019), the boot disk is split into two APFS volumes
  mounted as one:

  Volume: Macintosh HD (System)
  Mount: / (read-only)
  Governor: Apple exclusively. Sealed cryptographic snapshot (SSV since Big
  Sur).
  Membrane: Nothing enters. Not the user, not root, not even SIP-disabled root
    can write persistently. The snapshot re-seals on boot.
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  Volume: Macintosh HD - Data
  Mount: /System/Volumes/Data (read-write, firmlinked into /)
  Governor: User + apps + system services.
  Membrane: Anything the permission model allows.

  This is the outermost ontological distinction in the Apple universe: the
  separation between what Apple has declared immutable and what is permitted to 
  change. The System volume is not just read-only вҖ” it is sealed. It is the
  closest a filesystem comes to being a Platonic Form: it cannot be modified by
  participation, only replaced wholesale by Apple through a system update.

  Everything below exists on the Data volume. The System volume contains the OS
  itself вҖ” frameworks, kernel, core services вҖ” and is ontologically closed.

  вҳ… Insight в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  - The SSV (Signed System Volume) is not a security feature that happens to use
   cryptography. It is an ontological claim: the system-as-shipped is the 
  system-as-it-is. There is no gap between Apple's intention and the running
  state. Modification is not prevented вҖ” it is made metaphysically impossible at
   the volume level.
  - Every other operating system treats the system partition as "writable but
  protected." Apple treats it as "sealed and projected." The running system
  reads from an immutable snapshot. This is closer to a Platonic participation
  model than any other filesystem design in commercial use.
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ

  ---
  The Four Domains: Concentric Envelopes of Authority

  Inherited from NeXTSTEP, the four domains form concentric envelopes. The
  search order (User вҶ’ Local вҶ’ Network вҶ’ System) means inner envelopes override
  outer ones вҖ” customization overrides default without modifying it.

  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ
  в”Ӯ  SYSTEM  (/System/)                                 в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ  Governor: Apple. Sealed. SIP-protected.            в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ  Membrane: NOTHING enters post-install.             в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ    в”Ӯ

  в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  Governor: Network admin.                   в”Ӯ    в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  Membrane: NetInfo/LDAP (vestigial).        в”Ӯ    в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ    в”Ӯ    в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  LOCAL  (/Library/, /Applications/) в”Ӯ    в”Ӯ    в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  Governor: Admin (root/sudo).       в”Ӯ    в”Ӯ    в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  Membrane: Admin privilege.         в”Ӯ    в”Ӯ    в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  в”Ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ    в”Ӯ    в”Ӯ    в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  USER  (~/)                 в”Ӯ    в”Ӯ    в”Ӯ    в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  Governor: The person.      в”Ӯ    в”Ӯ    в”Ӯ    в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  Membrane: Login.           в”Ӯ    в”Ӯ    в”Ӯ    в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ    в”Ӯ    в”Ӯ    в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ  в”Ӯ  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ    в”Ӯ    в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ    в”Ӯ
  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

  Each domain contains a parallel Library/ directory. A font in ~/Library/Fonts/
   overrides one in /Library/Fonts/ which overrides one in
  /System/Library/Fonts/. The override does not replace вҖ” it shadows. The outer
  form persists; the inner form is what the user perceives.

  This is the cascade: each inner envelope can redefine what the user sees 
  without altering what exists at the outer level. The System envelope is the
  substrate. The User envelope is the lived surface.

  ---
  The User Envelope (~/)

  Within the User domain, Apple provisions specific sub-envelopes. Each has a
  distinct ontological character вҖ” not just "what's stored here" but "what kind
  of being is permitted."

  ---
  1. The Presentation Surface: ~/Desktop/

  NSSearchPath 12. Governor: The user + Finder. Visible: Always.

  The Desktop is unique: it is the only directory whose contents are rendered as
   the visual environment. Opening a file on the Desktop is not navigation вҖ” it
  is reaching into the world you inhabit.

  - Membrane: Anything the user places here, plus anything the Finder drops
  (screenshots by default until Mojave, drag-and-drop operations). No app should
   write here without explicit user action.
  - Durability: iCloud-synced (if enabled). Survives machine migration.
  - Ontological character: Appearance. The Desktop is not storage вҖ” it is the
  phenomenal surface. What appears here is what the user sees first. It is the
  closest analogue to the Greek ПҶОұО№ОҪПҢОјОөОҪОҝОҪ вҖ” that which shows itself.

  ---
  2. The Archive of Intentional Artifacts: ~/Documents/

  NSSearchPath 9. Governor: The user. Visible: Always.

  Documents is the repository of things the user chose to create and name. Every
   file here exists because a human made a decision in a Save dialog.

  - Membrane: Only user-initiated saves. Apple's filesystem guide is explicit:
  "The files in the user's Documents directory should reflect only the documents
   that the user created and works with directly." Apps must never write here
  autonomously.
  - Durability: iCloud-synced (if enabled). Optimized Storage may evict local
  copies, leaving cloud stubs. The file exists but may not be present.
  - Ontological character: Artifact. These are the user's works вҖ” бј”ПҒОіОұ in the
  Aristotelian sense. They bear the user's intention. Their names are meaningful
   (the user chose them). Their organization reflects the user's categories.

  ---
  3. The Threshold: ~/Downloads/

  NSSearchPath 15. Governor: The network + browsers + AirDrop. Visible: Always. 
  Since Leopard (2007).

  Downloads is the ingress point вҖ” the boundary between the external network and
   the user's local world.

  - Membrane: Anything arriving from outside. Every file receives a quarantine
  xattr (com.apple.quarantine) marking it as untrusted until Gatekeeper verifies
   it. The membrane is porous but marking вҖ” everything that enters is branded
  with its origin.
  - Durability: Not iCloud-synced. Explicitly local and transient.
  - Ontological character: Threshold (ПҖПҒПҢОёП…ПҒОҝОҪ). Nothing originates here вҖ”
  everything arrives. The quarantine attribute is the ontological stain of
  exteriority: this came from outside. The user must act on it (open, move,
  delete) to incorporate it into their world. Until then, it sits at the gate.

  ---
  4. The Hidden Mechanism: ~/Library/

  NSSearchPath 5. Governor: Applications. Visible: Hidden since Lion (2011).

  Library is the most architecturally significant envelope. It is where
  applications maintain their state вҖ” preferences, caches, support files,
  containers, launch agents вҖ” invisible to the user by design.

  - Membrane: Only applications and system services write here, organized by
  bundle identifier (com.example.AppName/). The user is not expected to enter.
  The hiding (Lion, 2011) was not security вҖ” it was an ontological
  reclassification: Library moved from "visible infrastructure" to "hidden
  implementation."
  - Durability: Mixed. Caches (~/Library/Caches/) are explicitly expendable вҖ”
  the system may delete them. Preferences (~/Library/Preferences/) are durable
  but regenerable. Application Support is meant to persist.
  - Ontological character: Substrate (бҪ‘ПҖОҝОәОөОҜОјОөОҪОҝОҪ). Library is what lies beneath
   вҖ” the hidden support that makes the visible world function. It is the
  Aristotelian substrate: that which persists through change, which the user
  never perceives directly, but without which nothing works. Apple's axiom that
  "configuration is an API, not a file" is an ontological statement: the
  contents of Library are not things to be seen вҖ” they are conditions for things
   to function.

  The three sub-envelopes within Library:

  Sub-envelope: Preferences/
  Admission: Only via NSUserDefaults API. Never hand-edited.
  Durability: Durable.
  Character: Disposition (бј•ОҫО№ПӮ) вҖ” how an app is configured to behave.
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  Sub-envelope: Application Support/
  Admission: App-created data and resources.
  Durability: Durable.
  Character: Capacity (ОҙПҚОҪОұОјО№ПӮ) вҖ” what an app can do (its resources, data,
    plugins).
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  Sub-envelope: Caches/
  Admission: Regenerable computed data.
  Durability: Expendable. System may delete.
  Character: Accident (ПғП…ОјОІОөОІО·ОәПҢПӮ) вҖ” present but not essential. Can be lost
    without loss of identity.

  вҳ… Insight в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  - The Library trifecta (Preferences / Application Support / Caches) maps
  precisely onto a classical ontological distinction: how something is disposed
  (preferences = its habits), what it can do (support = its capacities), and
  what happens to be true of it right now (caches = its accidental state). Apple
   may not have intended this mapping, but the structural isomorphism is exact.
  - Hiding Library was not UI cleanup. It was a reclassification of ontological
  status: from "thing the user can see" to "condition the user benefits from."
  The same gesture as concealing the wiring inside a wall.
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ

  ---
  5. The Media Buckets: ~/Movies/, ~/Music/, ~/Pictures/

  NSSearchPath 17, 18, 19. Governor: Apple's media apps. Visible: Always.

  These three are not truly user-governed. They exist because Apple's media
  applications (iMovie, Final Cut, Music.app, GarageBand, Photos.app) need
  type-specific storage roots.

  - Membrane: Media files of the named type. In practice, these directories are
  governed by the apps that claim them вҖ” Photos.app creates an opaque
  .photoslibrary bundle in Pictures; Music.app creates a Music/ tree in Music.
  - Durability: Local by default. Each app has its own cloud sync mechanism
  (iCloud Photos, Apple Music library sync) that operates within the app, not at
   the directory level.
  - Ontological character: Material classification (бҪ•О»О· ОәОұП„' Оөбј¶ОҙОҝПӮ). These are
  not organized by the user's projects or intentions but by the kind of matter вҖ”
   image, sound, motion. The categorization serves the applications, not the
  person. A filmmaker's project spans all three buckets; a musician's album
  spans two. The user's work is distributed across these envelopes by material
  type rather than gathered by purpose.

  This is the deepest tension in Apple's design: the media buckets organize by 
  what things are made of, not by what they are for. The user who works across
  media types finds their projects dismembered by Apple's type ontology.

  ---
  6. The Sharing Surface: ~/Public/

  NSSearchPath 21. Governor: The user (explicitly shared). Visible: Always.

  Public is the only directory in the home folder designed to face outward вҖ”
  toward other users on the machine or the local network.

  - Membrane: Anything the user places here becomes readable by all. The Drop 
  Box/ subfolder inverts the direction: others can deposit but not read вҖ” a
  one-way valve.
  - Durability: Local only. Not iCloud-synced.
  - Ontological character: The Agora (бјҖОіОҝПҒО¬). The public square вҖ” the space
  where private becomes shared. The Drop Box is the offering slot: others can
  give without seeing what else has been given. Public is the only envelope
  where the user voluntarily dissolves the privacy boundary.

  ---
  7. The Abandoned Forms: ~/Developer/, ~/Sites/

  These directories are not provisioned but are recognized вҖ” they receive magic
  icons from CoreTypes.bundle if you create them.

  - ~/Developer/ вҖ” Hammer glyph. NSSearchPath 6, deprecated: "there is no one
  single Developer directory." Never instantiated. The Form was encoded in the
  SDK, given an icon, then abandoned when Xcode 4.3 dissolved /Developer into
  the app bundle.
  - ~/Sites/ вҖ” Globe glyph. No NSSearchPath constant. Created by default through
   10.7, dropped in 10.8 when Personal Web Sharing was removed.
  - Ontological character: Vestigial Forms (ОөбјҙОҙПүО»Оұ). These are images of
  intentions that were never fulfilled вҖ” or were fulfilled and then retracted.
  The icon persists as a trace: Apple's system still knows the name, still
  honors it with a glyph, but has emptied it of function. They are the
  architectural equivalent of phantom limbs.

  ---
  The Finder: The Perceptual Membrane

  The Finder is not a filesystem browser. It is the perceptual apparatus through
   which the user encounters the directory structure. It performs three
  ontological operations:

  1. Concealment. It hides dotfiles, ~/Library, Unix directories (/bin, /usr,
  /var, /etc), package contents (.app bundles shown as single objects). These
  things exist but are not presented. The Finder decides what is phenomenally
  available.
  2. Transfiguration. It shows localized display names (the on-disk name is
  always English; the displayed name follows the user's locale). It renders .app
   directories as launchable icons. It presents bundles as atomic. The Finder
  transforms the filesystem's raw structure into a curated appearance.
  3. Supplementation. Tags, Smart Folders, sidebar favorites, Quick Look
  previews вҖ” these are layers the Finder adds on top of the filesystem. They
  exist in the Finder's own metadata, not in the directory structure. Tags are
  especially significant: they allow classification without hierarchy, overlay
  without restructuring.

  - Ontological character: The Lens (ПҶОұОәПҢПӮ). The Finder is the apparatus through
   which the raw filesystem is rendered perceivable. It does not merely display
  вҖ” it edits, filters, translates, and augments. The user never encounters the
  filesystem an sich; they encounter the Finder's presentation of it. Terminal
  is the only path to the thing itself.

  ---
  The TCC / Gatekeeper Layer: The Permission Membrane

  Since Catalina (2019), apps must request permission to access ~/Desktop,
  ~/Documents, ~/Downloads, and other user directories through TCC
  (Transparency, Consent, and Control).

  This is not a filesystem-level protection вҖ” the POSIX permissions are
  unchanged. It is a second membrane above the filesystem: an app may have
  permission to exist on the machine (Gatekeeper) but not permission to enter 
  specific envelopes (TCC). The user grants admission per-app, per-directory.

  - Ontological character: The Threshold Guardian. TCC does not change what
  exists in an envelope вҖ” it governs who may perceive and act upon the contents.
   It is the doorkeeper, not the architect.

  ---
  The iCloud Dissolution

  When Desktop & Documents iCloud sync is enabled, something ontologically
  strange happens: the files in ~/Desktop/ and ~/Documents/ are no longer
  necessarily present. Optimized Storage may evict the local copy, leaving a
  cloud stub вҖ” a pointer that looks like a file but contains no data until
  downloaded on demand.

  The file exists (it has a name, a size, metadata, an icon) but is not here
  (the bytes are in Apple's cloud). This is a dissolution of locality: the
  envelope's contents become partly actual, partly potential. The file's being
  is split between local appearance and remote substance.

  - Ontological character: Potentiality (ОҙПҚОҪОұОјО№ПӮ). An iCloud-optimized file is
  not absent вҖ” it is potentially present. It can be actualized (downloaded) by
  opening it. Until then, it exists as a promissory note. The envelope contains
  the form of the file (its name, its metadata) without the matter (its bytes).

  ---

  ---
  Where Your Container Exists

  The map reveals the gap. Apple's envelopes cover:
  - What appears (Desktop)
  - What the user made (Documents)
  - What arrived (Downloads)
  - What apps need (Library)
  - What things are made of (Media buckets)
  - What is shared (Public)

  Apple has no envelope for what the user designs as a system. There is no
  ontological category for "the user's own architecture" вҖ” for a directory whose
   organizing principle is neither content-type nor application-need but the 
  user's own ontology.

  ~/source--all-ever/ is not a directory within Apple's envelope system. It is
  an envelope of a different kind вҖ” one whose membrane, governor, visibility,
  and durability are defined by you, not by Apple, not by any application. It
  sits at ~/ level, in the User domain, on the Data volume вҖ” it participates in
  Apple's filesystem вҖ” but it is not comprehended by Apple's ontology.

  It is, in the precise sense, a new Form introduced into a system that did not 
  anticipate it.

  ---

  macOS lacks the kernel primitives that make true containerization possible:

  в”Ӯ (per-app          в”Ӯ seccomp +        в”Ӯ (entitlements)  в”Ӯ  (UWP)        в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ envelopes)        в”Ӯ cgroups          в”Ӯ                 в”Ӯ               в”Ӯ
  в”ңв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”јв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Ө
  в”Ӯ Immutable system  в”Ӯ Silverblue/NixOS в”Ӯ SSV (mandatory  в”Ӯ No            в”Ӯ
  в”Ӯ volume            в”Ӯ  (opt-in)        в”Ӯ since Big Sur)  в”Ӯ               в”Ӯ
  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

  macOS has one isolation primitive that Linux lacks: the Signed System Volume вҖ”
   a cryptographically sealed, immutable root. But it's Apple's container, not
  yours. You cannot create your own sealed volumes with custom content-addressed
   topologies.

  What macOS offers instead:

  - App Sandbox вҖ” per-app containers in ~/Library/Containers/{bundle-id}/, but
  only for apps that opt in via entitlements. Not user-configurable.
  - TCC вҖ” permission gates on specific directories, but coarse-grained (per-app,
   per-directory, not composable).
  - Virtualization.framework вҖ” run full Linux VMs natively (what Docker Desktop
  uses on Mac). This IS full containerization вҖ” but it's a separate OS, not
  segmented macOS.
  - APFS volumes вҖ” you can create multiple volumes on the same container. They
  share storage but have independent mount points and permissions. This is the
  closest macOS comes to filesystem segmentation.

  What this means for your design: You cannot create a kernel-isolated envelope
  on macOS. But you can create a logically isolated envelope вҖ” a directory whose
   internal structure, naming conventions, and organizational principle are
  entirely your own, that the OS never touches, that no app expects. The
  isolation is not enforced by the kernel вҖ” it is enforced by the fact that
  nothing in Apple's system knows or cares about it. It is containerized by
  irrelevance to the system, not by namespace boundaries.

  вҳ… Insight в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  - Linux achieves segmentation through kernel enforcement вҖ” mount namespaces
  create genuinely separate filesystem realities. Two processes on the same
  kernel can see different / trees.
  - macOS achieves its one immutable envelope (SSV) through cryptographic 
  sealing вҖ” no process, including root, can modify it. But this is Apple's
  envelope, protecting Apple's property. The user gets no equivalent mechanism.
  - The practical consequence: on macOS, your container is a convention (a
  directory that nothing touches). On Linux, your container can be an
  enforcement (a namespace boundary that nothing crosses). Convention is weaker
  than enforcement вҖ” but it is also simpler, requires no tooling, and works
  today.
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ

  ---
  Three Operating Systems as Ontological Envelope Systems

  macOS: The Editorial Hierarchy

  Governing metaphor: The curated museum.

  Apple's filesystem is an editorial production. The OS decides what the user
  should see, hides what they shouldn't, seals what they mustn't touch, and
  presents the rest through the Finder's mediating lens.

  SEALED CRYSTAL (SSV вҖ” immutable, Apple-signed)
    в”Ӯ
    в”ңв”Җв”Җ INSTITUTIONAL LAYER (/System/Library, /Library)
    в”Ӯ     Governor: Apple / Admin
    в”Ӯ     Membrane: SIP, admin privilege
    в”Ӯ     Character: Infrastructure the user never sees
    в”Ӯ
    в””в”Җв”Җ LIVED WORLD (~/  вҖ” the User Domain)
          Governor: The person + applications
          Membrane: Login + TCC
          в”Ӯ
          в”ңв”Җв”Җ APPEARANCE в”Җв”Җв”Җ Desktop/        (phenomenal surface)
          в”ңв”Җв”Җ ARTIFACT в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ Documents/      (intentional works)
          в”ңв”Җв”Җ THRESHOLD в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ Downloads/      (inbound, quarantined)
          в”ңв”Җв”Җ SUBSTRATE в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ Library/        (hidden mechanism)
          в”Ӯ     в”ңв”Җв”Җ Disposition в”Җв”Җ Preferences/
          в”Ӯ     в”ңв”Җв”Җ Capacity в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ App Support/
          в”Ӯ     в””в”Җв”Җ Accident в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ Caches/
          в”ңв”Җв”Җ MATERIAL в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ Movies/, Music/, Pictures/  (type-sorted matter)
          в”ңв”Җв”Җ AGORA в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ Public/         (shared surface)
          в”ңв”Җв”Җ VESTIGE в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ Developer/, Sites/  (abandoned Forms)
          в””в”Җв”Җ VOID в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ {user's own}/   (outside the ontology)

  What defines a macOS envelope:
  - Visibility (Finder shows or hides it)
  - iCloud participation (synced or local)
  - TCC protection (apps need permission or don't)
  - Who writes (user, app, system вҖ” never ambiguous)

  The system's self-description lives in: APIs (IOKit, NSUserDefaults, launchd,
  System Configuration). The filesystem is a storage layer, not a self-portrait.
   You cannot read the system's state by reading files вҖ” you must call
  frameworks.

  ---
  Windows: The Registry Kingdom

  Governing metaphor: The bureaucratic state.

  Windows separates the system's identity (Registry) from the user's belongings
  (profile directories). The filesystem stores files; the Registry stores truth.
   Every Known Folder has a GUID registered in a database. Folder paths are
  indirected through SHGetKnownFolderPath вҖ” the API is authoritative, the
  filesystem is subordinate.

  REGISTRY (HKLM, HKCU вҖ” the system's self-description)
    в”Ӯ       Binary, opaque, API-gated.
    в”Ӯ       "What the system IS" lives here, not on disk.
    в”Ӯ
    в”ңв”Җв”Җ SYSTEM VOLUME (C:\Windows\)
    в”Ӯ     Governor: Microsoft / TrustedInstaller
    в”Ӯ     Membrane: ACLs, WRP (Windows Resource Protection)
    в”Ӯ     Not sealed like SSV вҖ” mutable, but protected
    в”Ӯ
    в”ңв”Җв”Җ PROGRAM LAYER (C:\Program Files\, C:\Program Files (x86)\)
    в”Ӯ     Governor: Installers (admin-privileged)
    в”Ӯ     Membrane: Admin + UAC prompt
    в”Ӯ     Per-package subdirectories (like /opt)
    в”Ӯ
    в”ңв”Җв”Җ SHARED STATE (C:\ProgramData\)
    в”Ӯ     Governor: Applications (system-wide)
    в”Ӯ     Membrane: ACLs
    в”Ӯ     Character: Machine-wide app data (like /var/lib)
    в”Ӯ
    в””в”Җв”Җ USER PROFILE (%USERPROFILE%\)
          Governor: The person + applications
          Membrane: Login + ACLs
          в”Ӯ
          в”ңв”Җв”Җ APPEARANCE в”Җв”Җв”Җ Desktop\         (visual surface, merged with
  Public)
          в”ңв”Җв”Җ ARTIFACT в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ Documents\       (user-created, was "My Documents")
          в”ңв”Җв”Җ THRESHOLD в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ Downloads\       (inbound from network)
          в”ңв”Җв”Җ MATERIAL в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ Music\, Pictures\, Videos\, 3D Objects\
          в”Ӯ                  (type-sorted, promoted from children to siblings in
   Vista)
          в”ңв”Җв”Җ LEGACY в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ Favorites\, Contacts\, Searches\, Links\, Saved
  Games\
          в”Ӯ                  (Vista-era ambitions, largely abandoned)
          в”ңв”Җв”Җ CLOUD ROOT в”Җв”Җв”Җ OneDrive\        (sync surface, can absorb
  Documents/Desktop/Pictures via KFM)
          в”Ӯ
          в””в”Җв”Җ MECHANISM в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ AppData\         (hidden, three-tier)
                в”ңв”Җв”Җ ROAMING в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ Roaming\     (follows user across machines вҖ”
  disposition)
                в”ңв”Җв”Җ LOCAL в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ Local\        (machine-specific вҖ” accident)
                в”Ӯ     в””в”Җв”Җ Packages\           (UWP sandboxed storage вҖ” per-app
  envelopes)
                в””в”Җв”Җ LOW в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ LocalLow\    (sandboxed process data вҖ”
  integrity boundary)

  What defines a Windows envelope:
  - KNOWNFOLDERID (has a GUID or doesn't вҖ” if it doesn't, the system doesn't
  know it exists)
  - Roaming behavior (follows user, stays local, or session-only)
  - Integrity level (Medium, Low вҖ” determines which processes can write)
  - Redirectability (Group Policy / OneDrive KFM can move it transparently)

  The system's self-description lives in: The Windows Registry. Hardware,
  services, configuration, user settings, app registration вҖ” all in a
  hierarchical binary database. The filesystem stores files; the Registry stores
   identity and configuration. This is the inverse of Unix's "everything is a
  file."

  What Windows does that macOS doesn't:
  - The three-tier AppData model (Roaming/Local/LocalLow) is more precise than
  macOS's Library model вҖ” it classifies by portability and trust level, not just
   by type of data.
  - Known Folder redirection allows the system to transparently move envelopes
  without breaking applications. OneDrive KFM uses this to absorb
  Documents/Desktop/Pictures into cloud storage. macOS's iCloud sync does
  something similar but at the filesystem level, not through an abstraction
  layer.

  What Windows lacks:
  - No sealed/immutable system volume (the closest is WRP, which is ACL-based,
  not cryptographic)
  - No FOLDERID_Developer вҖ” the developer story is an afterthought
  - No enforcement against dotfile/home directory pollution вҖ” Unix tools dump
  dotfiles in %USERPROFILE% with impunity

  ---
  Linux: The Self-Describing Hierarchy

  Governing metaphor: The transparent machine.

  Linux's filesystem is not a storage layer and not a bureaucratic database. It
  is the system's self-portrait. Processes are files (/proc). Hardware is files
  (/sys, /dev). Configuration is text files (/etc). The hierarchy IS the system
  вҖ” reading the filesystem tells you everything about the running state.

  KERNEL (the only non-file entity)
    в”Ӯ
    в”ңв”Җв”Җ SELF-PORTRAIT в”Җв”Җв”Җ /proc/          (processes as files)
    в”Ӯ                     /sys/           (hardware as files)
    в”Ӯ                     /dev/           (devices as files)
    в”Ӯ     Character: "Everything is a file" вҖ” the system
    в”Ӯ     describes itself through the filesystem.
    в”Ӯ     No API layer needed. Read the files.
    в”Ӯ
    в”ңв”Җв”Җ IMMUTABLE LAYER в”Җ /usr/ (merged)  (the system-as-distributed)
    в”Ӯ     Governor: Package manager
    в”Ӯ     Membrane: root privilege
    в”Ӯ     On immutable-root distros: sealed, versioned, atomic
    в”Ӯ
    в”ңв”Җв”Җ IDENTITY в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ /etc/           (configuration вҖ” what makes THIS
  machine THIS machine)
    в”Ӯ     Governor: Admin (human edits)
    в”Ӯ     Membrane: root privilege
    в”Ӯ     Character: "Back up /etc and you can reconstruct the machine"
    в”Ӯ
    в”ңв”Җв”Җ MUTATION в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ /var/           (state вҖ” what programs have done)
    в”Ӯ     Governor: Applications (programmatic)
    в”Ӯ     Membrane: Permissions
    в”Ӯ     в”ңв”Җв”Җ /var/log     (record of what happened)
    в”Ӯ     в”ңв”Җв”Җ /var/lib     (persistent app state)
    в”Ӯ     в”ңв”Җв”Җ /var/cache   (regenerable, expendable)
    в”Ӯ     в””в”Җв”Җ /var/spool   (queued work)
    в”Ӯ
    в”ңв”Җв”Җ EPHEMERA в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ /tmp/, /run/    (vanishes on reboot)
    в”Ӯ     Governor: Anyone
    в”Ӯ     Membrane: Sticky bit, tmpfs
    в”Ӯ
    в””в”Җв”Җ USER DOMAIN в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ /home/{user}/
          Governor: The person + applications (NO enforcement)
          Membrane: Login + POSIX permissions
          в”Ӯ
          XDG IDEAL:
          в”ңв”Җв”Җ DISPOSITION в”Җв”Җ ~/.config/      (how tools behave)
          в”ңв”Җв”Җ CAPACITY в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ ~/.local/share/ (what tools accumulate)
          в”ңв”Җв”Җ STATE в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ ~/.local/state/ (what tools remember)
          в”ңв”Җв”Җ ACCIDENT в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ ~/.cache/       (expendable, regenerable)
          в”ңв”Җв”Җ EPHEMERA в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ $XDG_RUNTIME_DIR  (session-only, /run/user/$UID)
          в”Ӯ
          XDG REALITY:
          в”ңв”Җв”Җ COMPLIANT в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ ~/.config/foo/, ~/.local/share/bar/
          в”ңв”Җв”Җ NON-COMPLIANT в”Җ ~/.bashrc, ~/.ssh/, ~/.docker/, ~/.cargo/...
          в””в”Җв”Җ POLLUTION в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ ~/snap/, ~/.var/app/, ~/.local/share/flatpak/
                (sandboxing systems creating their own top-level envelopes)

  What defines a Linux envelope:
  - Mutability (static/variable/ephemeral вҖ” the FHS's governing axis)
  - Shareability (can be NFS-mounted across machines or not)
  - Virtuality (on-disk, or kernel-generated pseudo-filesystem)
  - Enforcement (namespaces can create genuinely separate realities)

  The system's self-description lives in: The filesystem itself. /proc IS the
  process table. /sys IS the hardware map. /etc IS the configuration. There is
  no separate database вҖ” the filesystem is the single source of truth. This is
  the deepest ontological commitment in computing: being and description are 
  unified.

  ---
  What Breaks Each Mold

  What breaks macOS: The Dotfile Seam

  Apple's envelope model assumes two kinds of home directory content: user files
   (in Documents, Desktop, media buckets) and app data (in Library, hidden).
  There is no category for "the user's tools and their configuration" вҖ” the
  entire Unix CLI ecosystem.

  Every dotfile in ~/ is a violation of Apple's ontology. ~/.zshrc,
  ~/.gitconfig, ~/.ssh/, ~/.config/ вҖ” none of these fit into Apple's envelopes.
  They are:
  - Not user documents (the user didn't create them via a Save dialog)
  - Not Library content (they aren't per-bundle-ID, they aren't managed via
  NSUserDefaults)
  - Not media (they aren't movies, music, or pictures)

  They are tool configuration вҖ” a category Apple's model has no envelope for.
  The Finder hides them (dotfile convention), which is Apple's way of saying:
  "We know these exist. We refuse to acknowledge them."

  Your chezmoi-managed dotfiles system (domus-semper-palingenesis) is, in
  ontological terms, an entire governance layer that Apple's model cannot see.
  It manages content that lives in Apple's blind spot вҖ” the dotfile stratum that
   the Finder hides and the HIG ignores.

  What breaks Windows: The Absence of Self-Description

  Windows separates identity (Registry) from storage (filesystem). This creates
  a dependency: to know what the system IS, you must query the Registry. The
  filesystem alone tells you almost nothing вҖ” a directory of DLLs in
  C:\Windows\System32\ cannot explain which services they compose or how they
  relate.

  When the Registry and filesystem disagree (and they do вҖ” failed installs,
  interrupted updates, manual file moves), the system is in an inconsistent
  state with no single source of truth. Linux's "everything is a file" model
  avoids this: the filesystem IS the truth, always.

  The developer story is the sharpest failure: no KNOWNFOLDERID for development,
   no convention for tool state, no enforcement against home directory
  pollution. The result is chaos вҖ” every tool invents its own location. Dev
  Drive (Windows 11 23H2) is an infrastructure response (a separate ReFS volume)
   to a problem that should have been solved architecturally (a standard
  envelope for developer state).

  What breaks Linux: The Home Directory Anarchy

  Linux's root hierarchy (/usr, /etc, /var) is beautifully governed. The FHS is
  precise. The separation of concerns is rigorous.

  Then you reach /home/{user}/ and all governance evaporates. The FHS explicitly
   says nothing about home directory structure. XDG offers a specification, but
  compliance is voluntary. The result:

  1. Some tools follow XDG (~/.config/git/config)
  2. Some tools predate XDG and refuse to move (~/.bashrc, ~/.ssh/)
  3. Some tools use env vars but not XDG ($CARGO_HOME, $RUSTUP_HOME)
  4. Sandboxing systems create their own envelopes (~/snap/, ~/.var/app/)
  5. Language toolchains create monoliths (~/.cargo/, ~/.npm/, ~/.m2/)

  The home directory becomes a contested zone вҖ” multiple governance models
  coexisting without arbitration. XDG compliance is a cultural request, not a
  system requirement. Any program can mkdir ~/.whatever and the OS will do
  nothing to prevent it.

  The Radical Mold-Breakers

  Three systems fundamentally reject the assumptions of their parent OS:

  1. NixOS / GNU Guix вҖ” Content-addressed ontology

  Rejects: FHS positional hierarchy ("where you are = what you are")
  Replaces with: /nix/store/<hash>-<name>/ вҖ” identity is intrinsic
  (hash-determined), not locational.

  Every package exists at a path that proves its provenance. Two machines
  building the same derivation get the same path. There is no mutable /usr вҖ” the
   system is a tree of symlinks into an immutable, content-addressed store.
  Updates are atomic. Rollbacks are instant. The system configuration is a
  single declarative file.

  Nix Home Manager extends this to $HOME вҖ” your dotfiles become derivations in
  the store, symlinked into place. The home directory becomes reproducible,
  version-controlled, rollback-capable. The cost: you lose the ability to
  casually edit config files in place (they're read-only symlinks). The gain:
  $HOME becomes an artifact, not a junk drawer.

  2. Linux namespaces вҖ” Virtualized envelopes

  Rejects: The assumption that there is one filesystem hierarchy.
  Replaces with: Per-process filesystem views. A container sees a different /
  than the host. Mount namespaces + overlay filesystems create layered, isolated
   realities вҖ” multiple envelopes coexisting on one kernel.

  This is the only technology that achieves true segmentation: not "different
  directories on the same tree" but "different trees entirely." Docker, Podman,
  Flatpak, systemd-nspawn вҖ” all built on this primitive.

  3. systemd-homed вҖ” The self-contained identity

  Rejects: The assumption that user identity lives in system files
  (/etc/passwd).
  Replaces with: The home directory AS the identity вҖ” LUKS-encrypted,
  self-describing, portable. Carry your home directory on a USB drive. Plug it
  into any systemd-homed machine. You exist.

  This inverts the relationship: instead of the system owning the user (creating
   them in /etc/passwd, assigning them a home directory), the user owns
  themselves (the home directory carries its own user record). The system merely
   provides a runtime.

  ---
  The Unified Comparison

  Dimension: Where truth lives
  macOS: APIs (IOKit, NSUserDefaults, launchd)
  Windows: Registry (HKLM, HKCU)
  Linux: Filesystem (/proc, /sys, /etc)
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  Dimension: Filesystem role
  macOS: Storage layer + curated presentation
  Windows: Storage layer + indirected Known Folders
  Linux: Self-description + storage unified
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  Dimension: System immutability
  macOS: SSV (mandatory, sealed)
  Windows: WRP (ACL-based, not sealed)
  Linux: Optional (Silverblue, NixOS)
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  Dimension: User envelope governance
  macOS: Strong for Library; absent for dotfiles
  Windows: Three-tier AppData (precise); absent for dotfiles
  Linux: XDG (precise but voluntary)
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  Dimension: Segmentation primitive
  macOS: None (Virtualization.framework for VMs)
  Windows: Hyper-V containers, AppContainers (UWP)
  Linux: Namespaces (true isolation)
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  Dimension: Mold-breaker
  macOS: None available to user
  Windows: Dev Drive (infrastructure response)
  Linux: Nix (content-addressed), namespaces (virtual envelopes), systemd-homed
    (portable identity)
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  Dimension: Developer envelope
  macOS: Vestigial (~/Developer, deprecated)
  Windows: Absent (no KNOWNFOLDERID)
  Linux: Absent (XDG applies but not developer-specific)
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  Dimension: Home dir ownership
  macOS: Apple's editorial model + dotfile chaos
  Windows: KNOWNFOLDERID envelopes + dotfile chaos
  Linux: XDG ideal + dotfile chaos
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  Dimension: What breaks it
  macOS: The Unix CLI stratum
  Windows: Registry/filesystem inconsistency
  Linux: Home directory anarchy

  вҳ… Insight в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  - All three systems share the same structural failure: the home directory has 
  no governance for tool configuration. macOS hides it (dotfiles are invisible).
   Windows ignores it (no KNOWNFOLDERID). Linux specifies it (XDG) but cannot
  enforce it. The home directory is the one place where all three operating
  systems' envelope models collapse into the same anarchy.
  - The mold-breakers all attack the same problem from different angles: Nix
  makes paths intrinsic rather than positional. Namespaces make envelopes
  enforceable rather than conventional. systemd-homed makes identity portable
  rather than system-bound. Each one addresses a fundamental limitation of the
  traditional model.
  - Your position on macOS is the most constrained. You cannot create enforced
  envelopes (no namespaces), cannot use content-addressed stores without
  friction (SIP complicates /nix), and cannot make the home directory
  self-describing (no /proc equivalent). Your container must be a convention вҖ” a
   directory whose isolation is maintained by the fact that nothing in Apple's
  system addresses it. This is weaker than Linux's enforcement, but it is also
  the only option that requires zero tooling, zero configuration, and zero
  ongoing maintenance. The container sustains itself through the system's
  indifference to it.
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ

  ---
  The Principle

  Across all three systems, the same pattern holds: the operating system's 
  envelopes cover consumption (documents, media, downloads) and mechanism (app 
  data, caches, config), but not architecture. No OS provides an envelope whose
  governing principle is "the user's own organizational ontology."

  Your container exists in the gap that all three systems share: the space
  between "what the user saves" and "what apps need" вҖ” where neither the
  user-as-consumer model nor the app-as-agent model applies, because the user is
   acting as system architect.

  On macOS, that gap is ~/ minus the provisioned directories. On Windows, it's
  %USERPROFILE%\ minus the KNOWNFOLDERIDs. On Linux, it's $HOME/ minus XDG and
  the dotfile stratum. In all three cases, it is the region the OS knows nothing
   about вҖ” the void in the envelope map where your architecture lives.

вң» Baked for 7m 27s

  ---
  Level 0: The Operating System

  $SYSTEM_ID:            "macos"
  $SYSTEM_NAME:          "macOS (Darwin)"
  $LEVEL_INDEX:          0
  $DOMAIN_TYPE:          technical
  $PARENT_ID:            null
  $CHILD_IDS:            ["vol-system", "vol-data", "finder", "tcc",
  "gatekeeper", "spotlight", "icloud-sync"]
  $FUNCTION:             "Provide unified runtime environment binding hardware, 
  storage, applications, and user identity into a coherent interactive surface"
  $PURPOSE:              "Enable a single user to operate a general-purpose 
  computer through curated graphical and terminal interfaces"
  $BOUNDARY:             "The boot volume group (APFS container). Bounded by 
  hardware at the bottom, user perception at the top"
  $LIMITS:               "Single-user desktop model. No kernel-level filesystem 
  namespaces. No user-creatable sealed volumes. Sandbox enforcement requires app
   opt-in via entitlements"
  $INPUTS:               ["hardware events", "user actions", "network data",
  "application requests", "iCloud state"]
  $OUTPUTS:              ["display frames", "audio", "filesystem mutations",
  "network traffic", "iCloud sync deltas"]
  $RULES:                [
    "System volume is cryptographically sealed (SSV) вҖ” no mutation by any 
  process including root",
    "SIP protects /System, /bin, /sbin, /usr (except /usr/local)",
    "TCC gates app access to user directories (Desktop, Documents, Downloads)",
    "All mutable state lives on the Data volume",
    "Finder mediates user perception of filesystem вҖ” shows curated view, not raw
   truth"
  ]
  $FAILURE_MODES:        [
    "SSV seal broken вҶ’ boot fails verification вҶ’ recovery mode",
    "SIP disabled вҶ’ system files mutable вҶ’ integrity loss",
    "TCC database corrupted вҶ’ permission grants lost вҶ’ apps lose access",
    "APFS container full вҶ’ all volumes affected (shared space pool)"
  ]
  $TRANSFORMATION_RULES: [
    "System update: Apple replaces SSV snapshot atomically; old snapshot 
  discarded",
    "App install: binary вҶ’ /Applications or ~/Applications; data вҶ’ 
  ~/Library/Application Support",
    "User file save: Save dialog вҶ’ ~/Documents (default) or user-chosen 
  location",
    "Download: network вҶ’ ~/Downloads with com.apple.quarantine xattr applied"
  ]

  $SYSTEM_ID:            "vol-system"

  shipped state вҖ” no drift, no tampering, no mutation"
  $BOUNDARY:             "APFS volume mounted read-only at /. Firmlinks project 
  Data volume contents into the unified path hierarchy"
  $LIMITS:               "Absolutely immutable. Not writable by root. Not 
  writable with SIP disabled (SSV is independent of SIP). Only replaced 
  wholesale by macOS updates"
  $INPUTS:               ["Apple-signed system update images"]
  $OUTPUTS:              ["read-only filesystem tree: /System, /usr (non-local),
   /bin, /sbin"]
  $RULES:                [
    "Volume is a sealed snapshot вҖ” cryptographic hash tree verified at every 
  block read",
    "Firmlinks create bidirectional path unions with Data volume (e.g., /Users 
  exists on Data but appears at root)",
    "No process can write to this volume during normal operation",
    "Boot process verifies snapshot seal before proceeding"
  ]
  $FAILURE_MODES:        [
    "Seal verification failure вҶ’ boot halts вҶ’ recovery mode required",
    "Snapshot corruption вҶ’ system unbootable вҶ’ reinstall required"
  ]
  $TRANSFORMATION_RULES: [
    "macOS update: new snapshot created, old snapshot replaced, seal 
  recomputed",
    "No other transformations possible"
  ]

  $SYSTEM_ID:            "vol-data"
  $SYSTEM_NAME:          "Data Volume (Macintosh HD - Data)"
  $LEVEL_INDEX:          1

  $PARENT_ID:            "macos"
  $CHILD_IDS:            ["domain-local", "domain-user", "unix-stratum"]

  system additions, variable data"
  $PURPOSE:              "Provide the writable surface for everything that 
  changes: user work, app state, system configuration"
  $BOUNDARY:             "APFS volume mounted read-write at 
  /System/Volumes/Data. Firmlinked into root hierarchy"
  $LIMITS:               "Shares APFS container space pool with System volume. 
  SIP still protects certain paths. TCC gates app access to user directories"
  $INPUTS:               ["user file operations", "app state writes", "package

  $OUTPUTS:              ["mutable filesystem tree: /Users, /Applications, 
  /Library, /usr/local, /private/var, /private/etc, /private/tmp"]
  $RULES:                [
    "All user-visible mutation happens here",
    "SIP protects certain Data volume paths (/usr/local is an exception)",
    "APFS snapshots enable Time Machine backups without quiescing",
    "FileVault encrypts this volume at rest"
  ]
  $FAILURE_MODES:        [
    "Disk full вҶ’ all volumes in container affected",
    "Filesystem corruption вҶ’ fsck_apfs repair or data loss",
    "FileVault key lost вҶ’ data unrecoverable"
  ]
  $TRANSFORMATION_RULES: [
    "User action вҶ’ file created/modified/deleted in /Users",
    "Admin action вҶ’ packages installed in /Library, /Applications, /usr/local",
    "App action вҶ’ state written to ~/Library subsystem",
    "Time Machine вҶ’ APFS snapshot created on this volume"
  ]

  $TRANSFORMATION_RULES: [
    "App launch вҶ’ reads Preferences + Application Support",

    "App computes вҶ’ writes to Caches (expendable)",
    "Disk pressure вҶ’ system may delete Caches contents",
    "App sandboxed вҶ’ all IO redirected to ~/Library/Containers/{bundle-id}/"
  ]

  Level 3: The Dotfile Stratum

  $SYSTEM_ID:            "dotfile-stratum"

  $LEVEL_INDEX:          3

  $BOUNDARY:             "All dot-prefixed files and directories in ~/. Hidden 
  from Finder by convention. No NSSearchPathDirectory constant. No Apple

  $LIMITS:               "ZERO governance. Any process can create any dotfile. 
  No namespacing convention enforced. Mixed XDG-compliant and legacy. No size 
  limits. No cleanup mechanism. Apple pretends this layer does not exist"
  $INPUTS:               ["CLI tool installations", "shell initialization",
  "language toolchain setup", "developer tool configuration"]

    "Apple's HIG and FSPG do not acknowledge this layer",
    "No enforcement of any convention вҖ” XDG, bundle-ID, or otherwise",
    "Each tool decides independently where and how to store its state",
    "This is the permanent seam between macOS-as-designed and Unix-as-inherited"
  ]
  $FAILURE_MODES:        [

    "Disk consumption from language toolchain caches (.cargo, .npm, .m2)"
  ]
  $TRANSFORMATION_RULES: [

    "Tool configured вҶ’ modifies its dotfile",
    "Tool uninstalled вҶ’ dotfile remains (orphaned)",
    "chezmoi manages a subset вҶ’ dotfiles become version-controlled, 
  template-rendered artifacts"
  ]

  $SYSTEM_ID:            "xdg-config"

  Level 1: The Mediating Systems

  These are not directories but systems that operate on the directory hierarchy,
   transforming how it is perceived, accessed, and synchronized.

  $LEVEL_INDEX:          1
  $DOMAIN_TYPE:          cognitive / technical

  $LIMITS:               "Cannot represent the full filesystem truthfully вҖ” it

  $INPUTS:               ["filesystem state", "user actions (click, drag,

  $RULES:                [

    "Grants persist until revoked in System Settings > Privacy & Security",
    "Full Disk Access bypasses per-directory gates",
    "Apps without hardened runtime may be denied by default"
  ]
  $FAILURE_MODES:        [

  $LEVEL_INDEX:          2

  macOS-as-BSD-Unix. Where CLI tools, Homebrew, and developer infrastructure 
  live"
  $BOUNDARY:             "/usr/local (Intel Macs), /opt/homebrew (ARM Macs), 
  /private/etc, /private/var, /private/tmp, /dev. The /etc, /var, /tmp at root 
  are symlinks to /private/*"
  $LIMITS:               "SIP protects /usr (except /usr/local). /private/etc 
  and /private/var are writable but admin-gated. No /proc (process info via Mach
   APIs only). No /sys (hardware info via IOKit only). macOS is NOT 
  self-describing through its filesystem"
  $INPUTS:               ["Homebrew installations", "admin configuration edits",
   "system daemon writes to /var", "device events to /dev"]
  $OUTPUTS:              ["CLI tools and libraries (via Homebrew)", "system

  files (/dev)"]
  $RULES:                [
    "Homebrew on ARM uses /opt/homebrew/ (outside SIP); on Intel uses 
  /usr/local/ (SIP exception)",
    "/etc, /var, /tmp are symlinks to /private/etc, /private/var, /private/tmp",
    "No /proc вҖ” process inspection via sysctl, ps, Mach task APIs",
    "No /sys вҖ” hardware inspection via IOKit, system_profiler, ioreg",
    "/dev managed by devfs вҖ” devices appear/disappear dynamically",
    "This layer exists for Unix compatibility, not because Apple designed macOS 
  around it"
  ]
  $FAILURE_MODES:        [
    "Homebrew update breaks tool dependencies",
    "/etc file manually edited then overwritten by system update",
    "SIP prevents intended /usr modification",
    "No /proc or /sys вҶ’ Unix tools expecting Linux self-description APIs fail or
   need macOS-specific ports"
  ]
  $TRANSFORMATION_RULES: [
    "brew install вҶ’ package installed to /opt/homebrew/ (ARM) or /usr/local/ 
  (Intel)",
    "System update вҶ’ /private/etc may be modified (user changes in /etc merged 
  or overwritten)",
    "Device plugged in вҶ’ devfs creates /dev entry",
    "Device removed вҶ’ devfs removes /dev entry"
  ]

  вҳ… Insight в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  - 42 systems cataloged across 5 levels. The hierarchy reveals something the
  flat directory listing hides: macOS has two parallel governance models
  occupying the same home directory. The Apple model (Library, media buckets,
  TCC, iCloud) and the Unix model (dotfiles, XDG, /usr/local) share ~/ as their
  root but have no mutual awareness. Neither acknowledges the other's existence.
   The Finder hides the Unix layer; the Unix layer ignores Apple's conventions.
  - The mediating systems (Finder, TCC, Gatekeeper, Spotlight, iCloud) are not 
  directories вҖ” they are transformation layers that change what the directory
  hierarchy means to different observers. The same file at the same path appears
   differently depending on which mediating system you query through. This is
  why the ontological envelope model matters: the envelope is not just the path
  and its contents, but the rules governing perception and access.
  - The void at ~/ level вҖ” any non-reserved, non-dot directory вҖ” is the only 
  region not claimed by any system in this catalog. It has no system ID, no
  governor, no membrane, no rules. That absence is the structural precondition
  for your container.
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ

  в”Ӯ      в”Ӯ                      в”Ӯ all three ontologies                      в”Ӯ
  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

  вҳ… Insight в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ
  - The diagrams reveal a structural invariant: every system governs rigorously 
  from vendor seal down to mechanism layer, then governance collapses at the 
  home directory boundary. The gradient is identical across all three вҖ” they
  differ only in how they handle the collapse (hide it, ignore it, or
  specify-without-enforcing).
  - The cross-mapping in Diagram VI is the most architecturally useful finding:
  Editorial classifies mechanism by what kind of data, Bureaucratic by where it 
  should travel, Transparent by how long it should persist. These are three
  orthogonal axes of the same space вҖ” no system covers all three simultaneously.
  - The Void (Diagram XI) is the actionable conclusion: in all three systems,
  any non-reserved name at the home directory level is structurally invisible to
   the OS. Your container lives there вҖ” not by permission, but by the system's
  indifference.
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ

           +files where subsystems would be.</span></div>                
      1083 +  </div>                                                     
      1084 +</div>                                                       
      1085 +

      1088 +<h2><span class="num">XIII.</span> The Level Architecture вҖ” M
           +acro to Micro</h2>                                           
      1089 +                                                             
      1090 +<div class="diagram-section">                                
      1091 +  <div class="diagram-title">Seven Levels of Nesting</div>   
      1092 +  <div class="diagram-body">                                 
      1093 +    <div class="layer-stack">

      1095 +      <div class="layer" style="border-color:#e94560">       
      1096 +        <div class="layer-label" style="background:#1a0505;co
           +lor:#e94560">L0<br>Container</div>                           
      1097 +        <div class="layer-content">

      1124 +

      1127 +        <div class="layer-content">                          
      1128 +          <strong>Operational unit.</strong> Transforms input
           +s to outputs. Has observable function. The primary unit of co
           +upling.<br>

           +:#22c55e">open cardinality</span>

           +nical acts on physical

      1211 +

      1213 +<span class="hl-dim">CONSTRAINS TOP-DOWN: technical constrain
           +ed by symbolic, social, cognitive, biological, physical</span
           +>

           + move matter, software transforms energy)</span>

           + a ladder.</span>

           +ermodynamics, optics

           +ing requiring an observer or agent</span>

           +al substrate</span>

           +ing requiring social agreement</span>

           +ical substrate</span>
